## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. Rate laws typically express dA/dt as functions of concentration (power laws, rational functions for catalytic mechanisms), with possible time dependence for non-elementary processes.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product concentration)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalyzes its own formation)
- Substrate inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential reactions)
- Time-dependent deactivation rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation over time)
- Fractional order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with baseline)
- Competitive pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (saturation-type rate law from quasi-steady-state approximation)
- Sigmoidal rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Rate proportional to concentration power → Power-law rate expression dA_dt = c*A**n, indicating nth-order elementary or apparent reaction
- Rate that decreases at high concentration → Rational function A/(1+c*A) or A/(1+c*A**2), indicating saturation or substrate inhibition
- Rate with both positive and negative terms → Reversible reaction dA_dt = c0*A + c1, equilibrium-seeking behavior
- Rate with product of concentration and (constant - concentration) → Autocatalytic mechanism A*(c-A), logistic-like consumption
- Explicit time dependence in rate → Non-autonomous kinetics from catalyst aging, photochemical variation, or coupling to hidden variables
- Rate with polynomial in A in denominator → Complex mechanism derived via quasi-steady-state approximation on intermediates
- Rate that changes sign → Reversible or equilibrium-approaching reaction where forward and backward rates balance
- Rate proportional to A times exponential in t → Coupled system where another species evolves exponentially and affects A's rate
